  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_9f31c70d-2c20-47d1-9d62-d9349a98c120'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer7781102300255352628">With what should have been the greatest heist of their career gone spectacularly sour, Locke and his trusted partner, Jean, have barely escaped with their lives. Or at least Jean has. But Locke is slowly succumbing to a deadly poison that no alchemist or physiker can cure. Yet just as the end is near, a mysterious Bondsmage offers Locke an opportunity that will either save</span>
  <span id="freeText7781102300255352628" style="display:none">With what should have been the greatest heist of their career gone spectacularly sour, Locke and his trusted partner, Jean, have barely escaped with their lives. Or at least Jean has. But Locke is slowly succumbing to a deadly poison that no alchemist or physiker can cure. Yet just as the end is near, a mysterious Bondsmage offers Locke an opportunity that will either save him or finish him off once and for all.<br /><br />Magi political elections are imminent, and the factions are in need of a pawn. If Locke agrees to play the role, sorcery will be used to purge the venom from his body - though the process will be so excruciating he may well wish for death. Locke is opposed, but two factors cause his will to crumble: Jean's imploring - and the Bondsmage's mention of a woman from Locke's past: Sabetha. She is the love of his life, his equal in skill and wit, and now, his greatest rival. <br /><br />Locke was smitten with Sabetha from his first glimpse of her as a young fellow orphan and thief-in-training. But after a tumultuous courtship, Sabetha broke away. Now they will reunite in yet another clash of wills. For faced with his one and only match in both love and trickery, Locke must choose whether to fight Sabetha - or to woo her. It is a decision on which both their lives may depend.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7781102300255352628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id='communityQuestionsWithAnswers'>
<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/848283-does-anyone-actually-like-sabetha-am-i">Does anyone actually like Sabetha? Am I the only one who just wants to slap the piss out of her? And Locke for that matter...Sabetha and Dena (Kingkiller Chronicles) make me want to strangle someone - worst love interests ever!</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_848283'><a id="like_count_community_question_848283" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/848283?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">25 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F2890090-the-republic-of-thieves">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/848283-does-anyone-actually-like-sabetha-am-i">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/848283-does-anyone-actually-like-sabetha-am-i">See all 15 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/25786179-octavia-pearce"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1583660983i/25786179._UY100_CR7,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/25786179-octavia-pearce">Octavia Pearce</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">She seems to get a bit of an unfair rap, maybe to do with the setting in which she's introduced? You expect her to be absolutely brilliant, but becaus<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">She seems to get a bit of an unfair rap, maybe to do with the setting in which she's introduced? You expect her to be absolutely brilliant, but because the majority of the book doesn't cover any actual political manoeuvring, and and the political manoeuvring itself isn't that clever or twisted, she comes across as a bit meh. If she was introduced as an opponent in a heist book as convoluted as the first or second book, and that book spent enough time focused on the heist, she would probably come across as crazy smart and badass. But instead this book focuses on Locke pursuing his feelings and she doesn't really get a chance to do anything impressive as a criminal. Instead we just get her feeling complicated things about the guy she fancies, which is realistic but not inspiring.<br /><br />For starters, having a complicated past, where people have wanted to kill and/or rape you for most of your life to date, probably doesn't help you build entirely stable relationships. It doesn't exactly help that the person she's interested in has completely undermined her. She's coming to terms with going from the most talented member of the group, to being second to a child younger and less mature than her, despite it seeming that the main reason he's managed to succeed at anything so far is by being small, unobtrusive and blooming lucky. She's demonstrating actual skill, but for some reason he's the one immediately groomed to be the leader. When she tries to point this out, he just doesn't get it, which doesn't help with her mood, and then people throw their hands up and go 'Jesus she's so moody for NO REASON it's so annoying'. Imagine if the positions were switched and Sabetha stole Locke's position as head of the group - he wouldn't be happy about it either and would probably mope around!<br /><br />She also probably feels pretty lonely as all the boys are Locke's allies, not hers. Locke ofc goes on and on about Jean being her friend, which he is, but if it came down to it Jean would pick Locke over her *every single time*, so again it probably feels to her like he's not really understanding what she's saying. <br /><br />The only thing that was really annoying was the scene where they talked about the red hair, but that just felt like a plot device so Locke leaves her and can get confronted, and for the end of the book. <br /><br />TLDR the setting doesn't give her the chance to shine, in the flashbacks she's annoyed that her talents are overlooked in her group just because a boy joined, that boy then doesn't understand why she got a bit miffed about it, and she has no best buddies to help her through and make her bad points look good.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1756527957" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1756527957" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1756527957?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575084469" href="/book/show/5660854-the-republic-of-thieves">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1756527957" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17925090276613851953"><b>3.5/5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Let me begin by saying that if I’ve read this book without knowing about Scott Lynch’s struggle with depression during this 6-years time of writing it, I’ll probably rate this book lower. This doesn’t mean that the book received a better rating from me because of his depression, but the knowledge did provide me with a better sense of understanding to the events that happened in this book, specifically to why some parts are infuriating to read and why there are times when the words he </span>
  <span id="freeText17925090276613851953" style="display:none"><b>3.5/5 Stars</b><br><br>Let me begin by saying that if I’ve read this book without knowing about Scott Lynch’s struggle with depression during this 6-years time of writing it, I’ll probably rate this book lower. This doesn’t mean that the book received a better rating from me because of his depression, but the knowledge did provide me with a better sense of understanding to the events that happened in this book, specifically to why some parts are infuriating to read and why there are times when the words he wrote really hit home.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I don't expect life to make sense," he said after a few moments, "but it could certainly be pleasant if it would stop kicking us in the balls.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>The Lies of Locke Lamora dealt with revenge caper, Red Seas Under Red Skies focus on heist and piracy, this installment revolves heavily around politics and the romance between Locke and Sabetha. The Republic of Thieves, the third book in The Gentleman Bastard Sequence series started strongly. The first 30% of the book was so great, and I thought it was actually shaping up to the best in the series so far, but sadly, the quality of the story fluctuates after that.<br><br>There were two issues within this book that stopped me from giving it a better rating. First, the plot. The plot still followed the storytelling structure of the series, this means that the narrative was told from the present and the past (interlude) time frame. It remains that way from the start until the end. The story begins 6 weeks after the end of the second book, a Bondsmagi approaches Locke and Jean, and the Bondsmagi offers an opportunity that will incredibly benefit both of them. But they must first succeed in rigging the election in the city of Karthain, the city of the Bondsmages, towards the Bondsmagi’s preference. <br><br>Unfortunately, the overall story felt lacking in quality, in my opinion. Once Locke and Jean reached the city of Karthain, the election-rigging and politics felt boring to read. Don’t get me wrong, I love politics in my epic/high fantasy reads, but the politics itself felt unimportant to the main overarching story of the series, and I was proven right by the statement of the characters themselves. Additionally, the main narrative of the interludes section deals with the characters reenacting a play called ‘Republic of Thieves, and again, they were uninteresting. There’s no intensity here; almost no sense of danger was felt throughout the whole book except in the first 30% and the last 10%. The iconic scheming of the series was still there, but some other crucial elements that made the series so good—Locke’s wits and the bromance between Locke and Jean—were scarce in comparison. This brings my review to the second issue I had with the book: the romance between Locke and Sabetha.<br><br>Since the first book, the name Sabetha has been mentioned often as this mysterious lover to Locke Lamora, and Scott Lynch did a great job building up expectations for her character. It’s safe to say, though, that my expectation leads to disappointment. Not only Sabetha was not as compelling as the other cast of The Gentleman Bastards, but she was also infuriating; for some reason, she reminded me of Denna from The Kingkiller Chronicle series. She’s smart and a definite rival to Locke in terms of wits and intellect, but she continuously treated Locke like crap, and yet Locke can’t help but still be madly in love with her. Once again, similar to Kvothe’s relationship with Denna. There’s probably a reason for this, but it’s not 100% confirmed yet. Regardless, I doubt it would change my opinion that it wasn’t enjoyable to read.<br><br><b>Picture: Locke Lamora &amp; Sabetha in Republic of Thieves <i>(Chinese edition cover)</i></b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1492363875i/22509628._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That said, although I disliked the portrayal of the romance, I do have to admit that their relationship was well-written. I can’t possibly say or confirm the author’s intention, but maybe Scott has always wanted the readers to feel Locke’s love and pain with Sabetha, and there could be a subliminal message in their relationship caused by Lynch’s divorce during the time of writing this book. I won’t spoil you on the details, but some of the passages did conjure a sadness in me; I may not like the romance, but I do think that Lynch has successfully poured his feelings articulately through Locke and Sabetha’s relationship.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“He said that life boils down to standing in line to get shit dropped on your head. Everyone's got a place in the queue, you can't get out of it, and just when you start to congratulate yourself on surviving your dose of shit, you discover that the line is actually circular.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b> <br><br>Now, hearing my issues with the book, you might be wondering why I still gave it 3.5 stars. Let’s move on to the positive aspects.<br><br>Excluding the main story, The Republic of Thieves was undoubtedly the best in the series so far in terms of providing characters exposure and characterizations to the crew of The Gentleman Bastards; I’ll say even better than the first book in the series. This was especially evident in the first 30% of the book, and pretty much the entire “interludes” sections. What made the first 30% of the book so good, to me, was because it displayed Locke's &amp; Jean's friendship. Locke and Jean will always have a place in my heart as one of the best duo of all time, along with Wax/Wayne from Mistborn Saga and Darrow/Sevro from Red Rising trilogy.<br><br><b>Picture: The Gentleman Bastards when they were young</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1492363875i/22509630._SY540_.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The amount of depth given towards Locke Lamora was stunning. His background, his personality, and his relationship development with the Gentleman Bastards were superbly written. It’s practically undeniable. Locke is an amazing character; this book shone so many lights towards the complexity of his character, and I honestly can’t wait to read more of his journey.<br><br>Finally, prose-wise, this is Lynch’s best writing so far. There are indeed less crude dialogues, and the story itself—in my opinion—wasn’t as entertaining to read, but by all means, this doesn’t imply that the writing was inferior. Looking back at what I’ve just read, there seemed to be noticeable differences in tone and story direction between the first and second half of the novel. Lynch himself did mention that his depression changed what he set out to write at first. Here’s an excerpt of the interview done by SF&amp;F with Lynch regarding his struggle with depression and why it took six years to write this book. The title of the interview is ‘Depression is a bastard.’<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I like to think that since I’m now a member of that tribe, I’m a little more cognizant about how I portray mental illness. But the depression isn’t reflected in it per se, everything else I frickin’ went through during those years is in that book, though.<br><br>Republic turned into a different book from what I started. That was the divorce. One of the most helpful things my mom said was that a divorce is like death. It’s like a third person in your life dies. And when I pulled myself back together and started writing again, I realized the story I was telling was not the one I started.” - Scott Lynch</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>I’m not an expert on this subject, I’ll just put one of Locke’s quotes as a message to you as an encouragement. To anyone who struggles with depression, this could be Lynch’s message to you.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Quit being so hard on yourself. We are what we are; we love what we love. We don't need to justify it to anyone... not even to ourselves.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Despite giving a 3.5 stars rating, The Republic of Thieves is still a great book. The rating reflects my disappointment more than the quality of the book itself. Although this is my least favorite installment in the series so far, this doesn’t mean that you shouldn’t read this book if you’re already a fan of the series. I personally think it’s amazing that Lynch was able to write three books with different settings, stories, and tones within the same series by using the same main characters. One last thing, there’s a high chance that the next book in the series, The Thorn of Emberlain, will be magnificent because The Republic of Thieves felt more or less like a setup for it to shine.<br><br><b>Picture: The Gentleman Bastard Sequence Book 1, 2 &amp; 3 collage.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1492363875i/22509629._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Full interview link: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://relentlessreading.com/2015/03/29/depression-is-a-bastard-how-scott-lynch-faced-his-demons-and-became-a-bestseller/">https://relentlessreading.com/2015/03...</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17925090276613851953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2067471000" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2067471000" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2067471000?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575084476" href="/book/show/5660855-the-republic-of-thieves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=4-star-reads">4-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2067471000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13479190494602751791"><b>
  <i>“You want a lesson, boy? If you find yourself being born, climb back in as quick as you can, because life’s a bottomless feast of shit.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>And isn’t that the truth? Locke Lamora has been through hell, and his life is about to get even more messy. After dealing with a dreaded Bondmagi in the <i>Lies of Locke Lamora</i>, and somehow surviving, Locke has found himself on borrowed time after his experience in <i>Red Seas Under Red Skies.</i><br/><br/>Pumping through his veins is a deadly poison. It is slowly eating away a</span>
  <span id="freeText13479190494602751791" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“You want a lesson, boy? If you find yourself being born, climb back in as quick as you can, because life’s a bottomless feast of shit.”</i>
</b><br><br>And isn’t that the truth? Locke Lamora has been through hell, and his life is about to get even more messy. After dealing with a dreaded Bondmagi in the <i>Lies of Locke Lamora</i>, and somehow surviving, Locke has found himself on borrowed time after his experience in <i>Red Seas Under Red Skies.</i><br><br>Pumping through his veins is a deadly poison. It is slowly eating away at his organs until nothing remains. His blood is trying to escape from his body, seeping through his eyes, his fingers and who knows where else. It’s a nasty way to go, and there’s no known cure. Sounds like the end of his thieving days until someone very unexpected offers him a deal in exchange for his life. A tempting offer, though even death sounds more appealing than working for such a nasty bunch of people. Locke’s a survivor though; he will take his chances and live to steal another day.<br><br><b>Let the game begin</b><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493002089i/22574703._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Here’s where the novel started to get real interesting. Told side by side with the main story, Lynch revisits Locke’s childhood once more. There was once a girl, Sabetha, someone who has haunted his steps since the day he met her. Locke is a charmer. As an adult, he is the kind of guy who can get anything he wants and anyone he wants if he really applied his mind to it. But he doesn’t. He’s only ever wanted one person. His love was strong, pure and enduring. And now he is about to face off against her as part of the deal he accepted. <br><br>On opposing sides of an election between the Bondmagi, each thief has been tasked with insuring that their respective party wins the day. They test each other’s wits, engage in underhand moves and try to remove their opponent in the most efficient of ways. The mages sit back and enjoy the show. No blood is allowed to be spilled so this very much remains a game of intellect between two equals. It became even more interesting as the sub-plot (how Locke and Sabetha first became romantically involved) is told along with it. Lynch really knows how to end his chapters on a powerful line that just keeps you hooked on the story. I stormed through this book as I wanted to see how the past shaped the future. <br><br>The romance plot was eloquently handled. Locke loves Sabetha, and he understands that she needs space and time, but what he struggles to understand is the fact that she is his equal as a thief. She doesn’t want to exist in his shadow. She wants to create her own legend, not be part of someone else’s. Time will bring them back together again, though I don’t think things will ever work out the way Locke wants. But that’s life.<br><br> This has easily been the strongest book in the series so far, I really look forward to seeing how it all develops in the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13479190494602751791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1972097841" />
    <a title="Lady Luna. ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53385361-lady-luna"><img alt="Lady Luna. ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575639837p2/53385361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1972097841?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lady Luna. ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lady Luna. ✨" href="/user/show/53385361-lady-luna">Lady Luna. ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53385361-lady-luna?shelf=cute-shit">cute-shit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53385361-lady-luna?shelf=great-books">great-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1972097841" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer316762066195551393"><b>4/5</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><br/>“False names are fun,” said Calo. “Call me Beefwit Smallcock.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>**this review contains mass amounts of quotes and fanart because I'm so inlove with these books and can't get enough. You have been warned**</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493002089i/22574703._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This is a tough review for me to write, mainly because I really love this series and consider it a favorite, so I had high expectations for this novel. However my expectations for this one were not met and I'm kinda disappointed. I really truly feel it is the weakest story in the se</span>
  <span id="freeText316762066195551393" style="display:none"><b>4/5</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><br>“False names are fun,” said Calo. “Call me Beefwit Smallcock.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><b>**this review contains mass amounts of quotes and fanart because I'm so inlove with these books and can't get enough. You have been warned**</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493002089i/22574703._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is a tough review for me to write, mainly because I really love this series and consider it a favorite, so I had high expectations for this novel. However my expectations for this one were not met and I'm kinda disappointed. I really truly feel it is the weakest story in the series so far. Why? Well this book was BORING. Don't get me wrong, I still really enjoyed reading it, but it wasn't that fun to read and I found myself losing interest. It was actually kind of a chore. I think the reason why I didn't enjoy this book as much, is due to the amount of politics and the fact that there is no complex scheme happening in the background, it didn't have its usual excitement. I personally just hated the fact that the whole novel was basically about Lockes obsession for Sabetha an election and a goddamn play. There was no heisty goodness or any badassery. Like there wasn't even a good FIGHT in this whole novel. It's fucking blasphemy. I swear, I nearly died of boredom. I do however understand the importance of this novel to the overall plot line. Yes it was boring, however it was good and informative. We found out a lot about Lockes past and we also finally meet Sabetha. We also find out Lockes real name*insert incoherent screaming*, this is honestly the thing I've looked most forward to all series. <b>So I still loved this special gem. </b>I understand that Scott Lynch started suffering from depression during the making of this novel &amp; that's also the reason the wait on book four has been prolonged. I have a lot of sympathy for depression suffers and I'm really proud of Scott, he still managed to write such an amazing story while suffering internally. And I hope him a quick recovery.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493002089i/22574704._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="700" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Three things must you kiss before I let you spook me for good. My boots, my balls, and my ass.”<br></i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>The plot is a continuation of the last story. Locke is poisoned and dying slowly. Jean has hired all the physikers to have him healed, however the poison has gone too far. A mysterious stranger turns up on the doorstep with a cure. However the price for the cure is to work for the Magi of Karthain. Who Locke and Jean have a rocky past with. Locke soon finds out that his beloved Sabetha is also working for the Magi. <i>So what will the Gentleman Bastards decide to do?</i><br>This is a tale of how Locke fell for Sabetha. It was quite cute like had me smiling so much my jaw was sore the next day and it was also extremely funny with LOADS of banter. So overall a okay book, I just hate romance and found this book to focus mainly on the romance, which just becomes boring for me, especially when you know how they end up because of the prior books mention of Lockes feelings for Sabetha. Speaking of Sabetha, I just have to say I really truly love Sabetha. I think she is amazing! I totally get why people hate her BUT I love her. I swear she's exactly like Locke only more snarky. She's perfection. Literally the most sassy character to ever exist.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493002089i/22574705._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="700" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><br>“I try to live by a cardinal rule of our shared profession, namely, ‘always leave a sucker wanting more.’ ”<br></i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I love flashbacks to Lockes past with Chains for a few reasons, a)because the sass is strong. <b>b) because of the Sanza twins. </b>I love them so much. Especially Calo💕. <b><br>“The hell you’ll do it,” said Calo. “You and that shaved head, you look like a vulture’s cock. This job calls for some elegance.”<br></b>. c) Chains is hilarious &amp; staunch. I love him <b>“Touch either of my children again,” said Chains in a tone of voice unlike anything Locke had ever heard, “and I’ll break you into so many fucking pieces not a whore in the city will ever be able to figure out which wrinkled scrap to suck.”</b> Seriously I'm so glad we had the flashbacks, if it wasn't for the Sanza twins and the whack shit they say, I swear I wouldn't have been able to finish this novel. Also there wasn't enough Jean in this novel! I love him &amp; missed him, yeah he was there but he didn't do much. Jean chapters are normally my favourite chapters.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493002089i/22574706._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="700" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Jean poured two glasses of wine and set one in front of Locke. He took a swig from his own. It tasted like something out of a tanning vat.<br>“Ah,” he said, “demonic ass-wash. Just the thing.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><b>The ending was amazing, especially the last ten pages. Like I wish the whole book was as exciting as that ending. Can book four, PLEASE HURRY UP. The suspense is already killing me.</b><br><br>Recommended to all fantasy fans. 15+ due to the amount of swearing &amp; fuckery.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><br>“More Camorri than you’ve ever seen in your fucking life. Not just us, or the other three currently toiling on your behalf on the other side of this pimple of a city. I mean big, unreasonable, cross-eyed motherfuckers straight out of the wombs of hell, and they’ll take you for a ride. Locked in a box, ten days, all the way to Camorr sloshing in your own piss.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493002089i/22574707._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i> All fanart used in this review is by <a href="http://kejablank.deviantart.com/art/Calo-and-Galdo-Sanza-Sketch-521016309" rel="nofollow noopener">Kejablank</a></i></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2856414734" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13314849398247487906">i couldnt help it. i was planning on waiting to read this closer to the release of book 4, but after <i>‘red seas under red skies,’</i> i just couldnt do it. i was desperate to know what happened next. <br/><br/>while this is my least favourite installment of the series thus far, that really isnt saying much because its still pretty amazing. i feel like the tone is different from the previous two books in that this is a much slower and less plot-oriented story. it definitely focuses more on the characters, their</span>
  <span id="freeText13314849398247487906" style="display:none">i couldnt help it. i was planning on waiting to read this closer to the release of book 4, but after <i>‘red seas under red skies,’</i> i just couldnt do it. i was desperate to know what happened next. <br /><br />while this is my least favourite installment of the series thus far, that really isnt saying much because its still pretty amazing. i feel like the tone is different from the previous two books in that this is a much slower and less plot-oriented story. it definitely focuses more on the characters, their relationships, and their pasts. <br /><br />i honestly dont mind this because there hasnt been much of this type of narration in the series so far, so i kinda feel like SL is playing catch up a bit with his character development. and the jury is still out on how i feel about the ever elusive sabetha. for being this mysterious woman, i wasnt exactly blown away by her, but i can appreciate what she brought to progression of the story.<br /><br />overall, this is still just as engaging, complex, and bastardly as ever!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1837517495" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1837517495" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1837517495?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1837517495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5753088091138510461"><b>By this point I fully confess I AM DOOMED TO LOVE EVERY BOOK IN THE GENTLEMEN BASTARD SERIES.</b> Doomed I tell you. Because it's hurting me but I'm so obsessed I can't stop???? And although this one is actually my least favourite of the 3 so far...it's still freaking 5 stars. So DOOMED, I say again, and then I fall on a heap on the floor because <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8074907.The_Thorn_of_Emberlain__Gentleman_Bastard___4_' title='The Thorn of Emberlain (Gentleman Bastard, #4) by Scott Lynch' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Thorn of Emberlain</a> doesn't come out till April and I'm suuuuuuffering with the waiting.<br/><br/>(NOTE: the cliffhanger isn't actually as bad as the last book's.</span>
  <span id="freeText5753088091138510461" style="display:none"><b>By this point I fully confess I AM DOOMED TO LOVE EVERY BOOK IN THE GENTLEMEN BASTARD SERIES.</b> Doomed I tell you. Because it's hurting me but I'm so obsessed I can't stop???? And although this one is actually my least favourite of the 3 so far...it's still freaking 5 stars. So DOOMED, I say again, and then I fall on a heap on the floor because <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8074907.The_Thorn_of_Emberlain__Gentleman_Bastard___4_" title="The Thorn of Emberlain (Gentleman Bastard, #4) by Scott Lynch" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thorn of Emberlain</a> doesn't come out till April and I'm suuuuuuffering with the waiting.<br /><br />(NOTE: the cliffhanger isn't actually as bad as the last book's.)<br />(NOTE #2: that doesn't stop me hungering for the next one so so badly that I'm climbing my bookshelf and screeching at the moon.)<br />(NOTE #3: status rabid-fan-level-10 acquired)<br /><br /><b>A BRIEF RUNDOWN OF THE CONTENTS OF THIS BOOK:</b><br />• it features politics because they get hired to rig an election<br />• it's also aaaaaall about Bonds Mages again! Not the Falconer, but just the bonds mages in general and it really surprised me how lowkey they generally were.<br />• Except oh boy do those bond mages go and mess with your brain 100% of the time and then THAT ENDING HOLY KELP IN A BARNACLE BOWL THAT ENDING.<br />• There is a plot twist that may or may not be true about Locke and his real identity and I'm dead.<br />• SABETHA IS BACK. Or, well, here for the first time. We've had two books of Locke thinking about her and BOOM she's an actual person.<br />• It does backflashes to Locke's childhood where he and the Bastard crew went on an acting sprint and it's hilarious and perfect and shows how he and Sabeth first fell in love when they were about 16.<br />• there is so much swearing and black humour and it's just perfect<br />• It's clever!! So much con artisting!!<br />• I'M ADDICTED.<br />• I LOVE THIS SERIES SO MUCH I CANNOT EVEN WITH JUST HOW MUCH I LOVE IT OKAY.<br /><br /><b>Jean and Locke continue to be epic bros.</b> They fight a LOT less in this book. And like book #2 is Jean's romance life, so book #3 is Locke's. Unfortunately Jean's idea of romance is like fighting enemies onboard a ship with wind blowing in your hair next to the love of your life as canons fire around them. Locke's idea, on the other hand, is falling on his face every time he sees his crush because CRUSH and then getting poisoned by her and he's not even mad.<br /><br /><b>If Locke Was In Mean Girls:</b><br /><br />Lock: one time Sabetha hit me in the face...and it was AWESOME.<br />Jean: *hits himself repeatedly in a brick wall and asks what he did to deserve being around Locke*<br /><br /><b>YEAH OKAY I ADMIT: I felt the romance sucked a lot.</b> The problem is: Sabetha. I did not like her, fiends. I did not. She has the "better than thou" attitude down pat. And Locke is just BONKERS for her and is a real idiot all the time around her and <i>it was so frustrating because he's smarter than this.</i> And she plays the game of "lead him on; smack him down" and takes any opportunity to run away from him...while still sending messages that she loves him. Like wut. Why. THIS IS NOT OKAY. If the romance positions were flipped and it was a girl weeping after a boy who lead the girl on -- it wouldn't be okay at all. <b>I did, however, end up somewhat shipping them.</b> But. Also...no. Locke/Jean 4EVA (They actually care about each other, dude.)<br /><br /><b>And also like, I enjoyed the story 99.9% OF COURSE because theses are my favourite boys.</b> But going from pirates on the high seas to politics was a definite drop for me. Mostly the politics were staging dastardly prank-ish wars...so it wasn't like confusing or anything. It was fun! It was full of schemes and cons! But. Pirates??? How can anything live up to tHE GLORY THAT WERE THOSE PIRATES IN BOOK 2. <br /><br /><b>But omg. Did I mention the freaking plot twists yet?!?</b> I'm so so so so floored. I cannot wait for book 4 so badly because I NEED ANSWERS ABOUT LOCKE'S PAST. (Also I know Locke's full name and it's hilariously terrible.)<br /><br /><b>OTHER THINGS I LOVED:</b><br />• how much I laughed<br />• like full on choking I was laughing so hard at the sass and quips<br />• which is awkward when one is listening to an audio FYI....people begin to think you're nuts<br />• the broship between Jean/Locke gives me life<br />• everyone constantly nearly dies and it's great<br />• backstabbing<br />• people playing people who are playing people<br />• so much info about the Bond Mages which was interesting<br />• Jean is hopelessly addicted to coffee and it's relatable<br />• Locke gets a prophecy that's freaking me out <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ "Key, crown, child"???? Okay so obviously Locke steals a lot of money, gets crowned king, he and Sabeth have a child, then he gets murdered so the fans never know happiness. #predictions <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />• DID I MENTION THE LEVELS OF SASS AND THIEVERY MY TWO FAVOURITE THINGS<br /><br /><br /><b>Basically the Gentleman Bastards are the actual best series that's happened to me in a long time.</b> It's so firmly on my top-favourites-shelf that I think it's glued there. Forever. &lt;3 I'm just crying becauseI love it so much and there's like 4+ years between book releases. Thanks for nothing, Cait, for starting an epic fantasy series with a slow author. You deserve this pain, YOU THOUGHTLESS GUMNUT.<br /><br />Now excuse me while I go shout my feelings into the void of WHY HAVE I FINISHED ALL THE AVAILABLE BOOKS AND I WANT MORE.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5753088091138510461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575084476" href="/book/show/5660855-the-republic-of-thieves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=500-page-plus">500-page-plus</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer12729424320507658485"><i> "Hardship is boring as all hell. Gotta find laughs if you can't stay drunk." </i><br/><br/>What a great fantasy series this is! I did find this one ever so slightly harder to tackle, it's a good 100 pages longer than book 2 and a lot of the content was quite political and less fast moving.<br/><br/>Locke and Jean have managed to escape their latest escapade on the high seas and are now firmly back on land. Before long they have been swept up by the Bondsmagi and forced into another heist filled with deception and tric</span>
  <span id="freeText12729424320507658485" style="display:none"><i> "Hardship is boring as all hell. Gotta find laughs if you can't stay drunk." </i><br /><br />What a great fantasy series this is! I did find this one ever so slightly harder to tackle, it's a good 100 pages longer than book 2 and a lot of the content was quite political and less fast moving.<br /><br />Locke and Jean have managed to escape their latest escapade on the high seas and are now firmly back on land. Before long they have been swept up by the Bondsmagi and forced into another heist filled with deception and trickery.<br />The narrative switches between the present day, and flashbacks to when the Gentleman's Bastards were young and given an important task by father chains, to become part of a group of players, and learn to work together.<br />We finally get to meet Sabetha in this book - which is great as we'd heard so much about her in the first two books. Her on/off relationship with Locke kept me on edge, particuarly when it turns out that Sabetha had also been hired by the Bondsmagi to compete against Locke and Jean.<br /><br />With all the double crossing and secret keeping we have come to expect from Locke Lamora, there is plenty to keep the reader interested. So much intricate world building, and a big twist at the end.<br />I'm not sure how long we will be waiting for book 4, so I may reread the first 3 before that happens.<br /><br /><i> "I don't expect life to make sense...but it would certainly be pleasant if it would stop kicking us in the balls." </i></span>

<div id="review_2198522176" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2198522176" />
    <a title="Dana Ilie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21690081-dana-ilie"><img alt="Dana Ilie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584606424p2/21690081.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2198522176?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana Ilie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana Ilie" href="/user/show/21690081-dana-ilie">Dana Ilie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21690081-dana-ilie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2198522176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4516542814385750339">I LOVED the flashbacks in the The Lies of Locke Lamora, and I LOVED seeing the gentlemen bastards all working and interacting with each other. In Red Seas Under Red Skies, those flashback were only there for a little bit, and I severely missed seeing all the bastards together! Not this time though! In The Republic of Thieves, we have a full book of interlude flashbacks that contain all the original members of the gentleman bastard… include Sabetha!<br/>The flashback this time dealt, at first, with ho</span>
  <span id="freeText4516542814385750339" style="display:none">I LOVED the flashbacks in the The Lies of Locke Lamora, and I LOVED seeing the gentlemen bastards all working and interacting with each other. In Red Seas Under Red Skies, those flashback were only there for a little bit, and I severely missed seeing all the bastards together! Not this time though! In The Republic of Thieves, we have a full book of interlude flashbacks that contain all the original members of the gentleman bastard… include Sabetha!<br />The flashback this time dealt, at first, with how Locke and Sabetha first met – how Locke was such a little school-boy trying to talk to and impress her – to suddenly everyone goes to a theatre pretending to be actors to start in the play, The Republic of Thieves.<br /><br />In The Republic of Thieves, the framework of the past operates around Locke and Sabetha's shared history, while the present is a competition over elections in a foreign country, the Bondsmagi's backyard. And it really is a competition, an utterly hilarious one as Locke and Sabetha strive against and with each other, smacking you in the face with how ridiculous politics in elections become.<br /><br />We get more of the mysterious creepers that are the Bondsmagi with alarming implications of what's to come in future books. We get more of Jean Tannen, and he keeps pushing Locke, too. We get horrifying situations and the characters' wit has me snickering through them. We get an ending that is bittersweet and perfect.<br />I have to say: its incredible reading how Locke’s characters has changed over these three books! The Locke I first met in Lies and as a child with Chains, is nothing like the Locke we see in this book. Heck, the Locke at the start and end is different! But what’s so incredible is, through all of Locke’s character personality and motive, not once I have question how he did this or why he suddenly believes that.<br /><br />Fans of the series know how much of a rollercoaster life has taken Locke on, but somehow, Scott has made it all make sense. Not one time have I ever questions one word, action, motive, or choice that Locke has made – or any character for that matter!<br /><br />The Republic of Thieves packs a punch or three, and it's fun besides. It's not what I was expecting, but I'm delighted with what we got.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4516542814385750339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_128618291" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/128618291" />
    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4058409-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521048822p2/4058409.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/128618291?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/4058409-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4058409-susan?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4058409-susan?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4058409-susan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4058409-susan?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4058409-susan?shelf=af">af</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4058409-susan?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128618291" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4144387033526361894">(This review doesn’t really contain spoilers until the second part, when I say there are spoilers. However, some vague information about earlier books is drawn upon in the first part. If you’re being cautious, don’t read this review.)<br/><br/><b>Upon first discovering its impending release...</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380325786i/691081._SX540_.jpg' width='500' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>Sabetha?!</i><br/><br/>...Wait. Wait, you mean we actually get to <i>meet</i> Sabetha?<br/><br/>Well, Jesus. I've been wanting to meet this 'Sabetha' forever. If she's the reason Locke is both obsessed with and wary of red-heads, I want to know who s</span>
  <span id="freeText4144387033526361894" style="display:none">(This review doesn’t really contain spoilers until the second part, when I say there are spoilers. However, some vague information about earlier books is drawn upon in the first part. If you’re being cautious, don’t read this review.)<br><br><b>Upon first discovering its impending release...</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380325786i/691081._SX540_.jpg" width="500" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Sabetha?!</i><br><br>...Wait. Wait, you mean we actually get to <i>meet</i> Sabetha?<br><br>Well, Jesus. I've been wanting to meet this 'Sabetha' forever. If she's the reason Locke is both obsessed with and wary of red-heads, I want to know who she is. If saying 'What would <i>Sabetha</i> think of you, right now?' can shock Locke out of a depressed stupor, I want to know why. If he swoons upon thought of her, grimaces upon hearing her name, and gets defensive upon mention of his feelings towards her...well, you get the picture. I want to know who the frick this woman is to be able to make <i>the</i> Bastard a gibbering mess of self-pity.<br><br>Locke's match in skill and wit? <i>Really?</i> There actually <i>is</i> such a thing?<br>I suppose for someone as vain as our dear Locke, his infatuation must be just so.<br><br>Now... he will oppose her? I'm not sure if I'm excited for him, or if I feel <i>bad</i> for him.<br><br>We haven't even seen her 'in scene' in any of the reminiscences. Just her name mentioned, her whereabouts just partially revealed, or something vaguely said about her general appearance. We know for sure that Locke finds her attractive. She is the only female Gentleman- excuse me- <i>Lady</i> Bastard. She's done <i>some</i>thing unforgivable, though it is unclear what. We know she is far, far away. We know that she's a genius (a freaking MATCH IN WITS with our dear Locke). She is the <i>Rose</i> of Camorr, whereas Locke is the Thorn. She's most likely older than him, as Chains mentions signs of puberty appearing in her much earlier than in Locke. She's a red-head, which isn't a secret. She's mad, insane, as according to anyone who had ever met her. Locke still loves her... or her memory at least, I suppose.<br><br>I'm going to assume she is nearly identical in personality to Mr. Lamora. Mostly because, well, Locke is a self-obsessed narcissist at times. Sure he's had his moments of self-judgement. But mostly he's a conceited asshole. I'm not saying we don't love him for it, I'm just listing facts.<br><br>I'm also going to assume that when Locke lays eyes on her again, Jean will have to hold up his slack, inanimate body. I'm just guessing, but you have to agree that it's rather logical: take into consideration both Locke's image of her as described by Lynch, and some of Lynch's character reaction tendencies, and there you go. Consider it a theory.<br><br>I'm excited, if you didn't pick that up already.<br><br><b>Edit 8/6/12:</b><br>God, I hope it's really coming out this month. Oh, Lord, I pray to thee...<br><br><b>Edit Later:</b><br>Whatdayaknow? It's not.<br><br><b>Edit Even Later:</b><br>GODDAMMIT, LYNCH.<br><br><b>Edit Even Even Later:</b><br>Oooooh, so now it's coming out October <i>this</i> year, 2013? I'm almost afraid to hope so.<br>But I really, really hope so.<br><br><b>Edit Much Later:</b><br>YEEEEEESSSSS IIIIII HAAAAAAAAVVVVVVEEEEEE IIIIIITTTTTTTTTT!<br><br><br><b>Edit Upon Finishing:</b><br>Oh. My. God.<br>It wasn't a love story (love stories make me angry) but it was just right in that it portrayed love, but still kept it in the background of the overall story.<br>And when the book DID reveal it and decided to play with it a little bit, the story reached heavenly proportions. Oh my God.<br><br><b>Spoiler-free overview:</b><br>The Story:<br>He's in love.<br>But his 'long-ago-lover' left him years and years ago. However, when he finally joins her again, she is his enemy by design.<br>They are working against each other, much as they did in childhood (revealed through Interludes), to achieve opposing ends.<br>And in the end, Locke's true ancestry is revealed.<br>(There is brief foreshadowing of his ancestry, by the way... you may catch it).<br><br>The Interludes:<br>Sabetha was Locke's first Minder, an older child assigned to himself and some others as an overseer during his earlier childhood.<br>Upon first sight, when she spoke her first word to him, he fell in love (though he didn't know this yet).<br>Later in life, they are both assigned to Chains, and as they age, things become more complicated between them.<br>Eventually, Chains sends them away during these 'awkward years,' to get a hold of themselves and relearn to work together as a team, rather than argue like old men and women.<br>They are sent away to work for a man named Jasmer Moncraine, an actor, head of the Moncraine Company, preparing to preform a play entitled 'The Republic of Thieves.'<br>And despite the fact that this goes horribly wrong, the group of young Brother (and Sister) Bastards do become reliant on each other, once more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4144387033526361894" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1922316088" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1922316088" />
    <a title="Adina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22189348-adina"><img alt="Adina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531917330p2/22189348.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1922316088?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adina" href="/user/show/22189348-adina">Adina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22189348-adina?shelf=fantasy-sf">fantasy-sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1922316088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10194153833949734373">2.5*- 3* RTC<br/><br/>I was in love with the first book in the series, The Lies of Locke Lamora. Everything about it made me jump with joy while reading, even the gory parts. I loved the characters, the cussing, the banter between the characters, the dark side of Locke’s mind, even the never ending world building. On to Red Seas Under Red Skies. I still enjoyed it a lot even though more than half was set on the sea and I am not a fan of seafaring. Still, the plot was interesting, Locke and Jean were as fu</span>
  <span id="freeText10194153833949734373" style="display:none">2.5*- 3* RTC<br /><br />I was in love with the first book in the series, The Lies of Locke Lamora. Everything about it made me jump with joy while reading, even the gory parts. I loved the characters, the cussing, the banter between the characters, the dark side of Locke’s mind, even the never ending world building. On to Red Seas Under Red Skies. I still enjoyed it a lot even though more than half was set on the sea and I am not a fan of seafaring. Still, the plot was interesting, Locke and Jean were as fun as ever and the ending did not disappoint. <br /><br />The Republic of Thieves, on the other hand, was a disappointment. I postponed reading it because I was expecting a fail based on my friends reviews and the author’s state of mind when he wrote the novel. Scott Lynch suffers from severe anxiety and depression and wrote TROT while going through a divorce. You can clearly see that he was unwell in his writing, by its bleakness and lack of spark. I am sorry for him, I hope he recovers and manages to continue the series but I will not give extra points for sympathy. I will write my reviews for the content of what I’m reading. <br /><br />Why was I so disappointed? Let’s start with the plot. It was boring, stale and the resolution lacked the spark of genius that the other two volumes had. In short and spoiler free, Locke and Jean are hired (coerced) by half of the Bondsmagi to help them win/rig an election between two parties. Surprise, the opposition hires Sabetha counter Locke’s efforts. We finally get to meet the infamous love of Locke’s life and they are supposed to be fighting with each other. It should have been amazing, fireworks should fly around, I shouldn’t have been able to put the book down. Sadly, that did not happen. The whole election intrigue was lacking any life and I sort of just wanted to end. <br /> Next, the love story. We waited for 1200 pages or so to meet Sabetha and when we did it was so anticlimactic and lame. I could not see any chemistry between the two of them although the author tried hard to create some. Locke felt a bit pathetic with his puppy-love attitude and his willingness to suffer continuously because of love. <br /><br />Thirdly, the side story which covers about half of the book. We are taken back in time when the crew was still together and younger. They are sent by Father Chains to play in an itinerant theater company outside Camorr and there they are faced with a number of challenges. We also get the chance to see how Sabetha and Locke got together. Sadly, this part was a boring as the other onet and again there was no chemistry between the two lovebirds. <br /><br />The first 100 pages and the last 100 saved the novel for me but it wasn’t enough to make it a good read. I will continue with the series if the author ever gets to finish the next one (which I doubt) but I will not hold my hopes too high.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10194153833949734373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2711369769" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2711369769?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/18715886-the-republic-of-thieves">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Matthew by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/38754821-mike">Mike</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2711369769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3720356996059080367">This first book in this series was very good.<br/><br/>The second book in this series was excellent!<br/><br/>This book was just meh . . .<br/><br/>Each one of the books is a similarly meandering and complex epic adventure with twists, turns, and surprises. The Republic of Thieves was no exception. The problem was that I could not really get invested in either of the main storylines. The previous books were true adventures while these stories just felt like ho –hum, day in the life type stuff. <br/><br/>I will say that if you like the</span>
  <span id="freeText3720356996059080367" style="display:none">This first book in this series was very good.<br /><br />The second book in this series was excellent!<br /><br />This book was just meh . . .<br /><br />Each one of the books is a similarly meandering and complex epic adventure with twists, turns, and surprises. The Republic of Thieves was no exception. The problem was that I could not really get invested in either of the main storylines. The previous books were true adventures while these stories just felt like ho –hum, day in the life type stuff. <br /><br />I will say that if you like the characters and the writing in the first two books, you will find more of the same here. That makes this definitely a must read for those who have enjoyed the series so far. But, for me it will just be for the sake of connecting book two to book four – which will hopefully return to a much more exciting and riveting adventure.<br /><br />Now, before you take my words to heart, note that this book is highly rated on Goodreads so it does appear that many did not have the same feelings I did. Perhaps you will fall into that category – and I hope you do! But, be prepared to possibly have the same experience I had. <br /></span>
