    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_629132201" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/629132201" />
    <a title="AnHeC the Paperback Obliterator" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20781309-anhec-the-paperback-obliterator"><img alt="AnHeC the Paperback Obliterator" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384719838p2/20781309.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/629132201?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AnHeC the Paperback Obliterator" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AnHeC the Paperback Obliterator" href="/user/show/20781309-anhec-the-paperback-obliterator">AnHeC the Paperback Obliterator</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer629132201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer561770931624784467"><b>Word count: about 250 000 or something, just a rough estimate<br/>Rating: Bouncing around like a unicorn on a pogo stick + why do you keep on hitting me in the face with a brick while I'm trying to have fun? = (yes, you've guessed it) MIND NUMBING CONCOCTION OF AWESOME AND HORRID.<br/> </b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379797432i/631670.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>I'm sorry, but there is no way to keep it brief. </b><br/><br/>First of all, it’s a long book. Yes, reading it undeniably takes a while, but <b>I’ve very much enjoyed it in general. </b>Don’t let the length discourage you from picking that one </span>
  <span id="freeText561770931624784467" style="display:none"><b>Word count: about 250 000 or something, just a rough estimate<br>Rating: Bouncing around like a unicorn on a pogo stick + why do you keep on hitting me in the face with a brick while I'm trying to have fun? = (yes, you've guessed it) MIND NUMBING CONCOCTION OF AWESOME AND HORRID.<br> </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379797432i/631670.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I'm sorry, but there is no way to keep it brief. </b><br><br>First of all, it’s a long book. Yes, reading it undeniably takes a while, but <b>I’ve very much enjoyed it in general. </b>Don’t let the length discourage you from picking that one up! (There are bigger problems)<br><br>Most of the time I was like:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380423583ra/843920.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>How is it constructed? <b>The action flashes between events of the past</b>, when Gentleman Bastards were children <b>and current timeline</b>. Usually that turns into a mess with one of the aspects a boring drudgery, a torturous parts you suffer only to get to the ‘good stuff’. You know what I’m talking about, right? Well, that is not the case here. I still can’t decide which story (the past or the present) I enjoyed more. <b>Both were thoroughly entertaining, which is uncommon. </b> (Yes, despite all my problems with it, I did have fun. At least until I got fed up with both storylines.)<br><br><b>The bit concerning events of the past focuses on the time before Locke Lamora became a masterful, thieving mastermind. </b>We get to see a boy of 6 or 7; see him get older and grow into his own skin. He wasn’t born perfect. We see him making mistakes, stumbling, being unreasonable or naïve. Locke Lamora the Wicked Mastermind (version in progress). We get to see Gentleman Bastards before they became a real brotherhood. And finally we learn a story of their first lone endeavour that cemented their bonds and made full use of the abilities instilled in them by Chains over the course of many years. <b> It was an exciting ride. </b> Even if a bit annoying at times (Sabetha, she really gets on my nerves) <br><br><b>The plot centred around the events of ‘now’? </b> It did lack the big UMPH at the end, because the main story… isn’t the main story? I don’t even know how to say it. But the big current adventure of the book isn’t what it was all about. So that was to be expected. <b>It’s more about characters (namely Sabetha and Locke) and their past vs. current relationship far more than the proverbial ‘big heist’ </b> (ok, I know ‘big heists’ are not proverbial, but hey, you know what I mean). The goings on between Jean, Sabetha, and Lock; that’s what it was focused on. Not the ‘thieving action’. It’s good or bad depending how you look at it. Now, I love all the scheming in the dark, the pretend game, the risk, so it would be a big minus for me, even though <b>I’m already emotionally invested in the characters, which means it kept me on the edge of my seat, hungry for every single word. (at least for a while, until I realized the excellent parts I love aren't going to come. Ever.) </b><br><br><b>CHARACTERS:<br>THEY MAKE THOSE BOOKS! </b><br><br><b>Sabetha:</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380423583ra/843921.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I’ll start with a negative, to get it out of the way. One word. INFURIATING. She’s a one, stuck-up bitch. I didn’t like her. She’s annoying, selfish, jealous, thinks she should be the centre of the world. Her favourite past time seems to be dissecting; her own feelings, relationships with others, inner workings of Gentleman Bastards, you name it. She’ll dissect it and have issues with it. Always finding something to be angry about (preferably angry at Locke, because hey, nothing makes carrying on easier than misplaced blame!) She’s obsessed with the thought that Lock only wants her, only ever wanted her, for one reason only. She’s been making him run in circles around that issue for YEARS! <b>He’s all meek and nice and apologetic while he should put his foot down and tell her to just fuck off. </b><br><br><b>So I don’t like Sabetha, yet she’s an <s>enjoyable</s> interesting enough character. </b> Reading about her and Lock was... kind of torture/ kind of fun. It showed him in a different light, and her… well, let’s just say she matters to the story (both stories, actually). But if we were supposed to like her, then Scott Lynch failed. I hated her by the end. I'm just saying that sometimes you're supposed to feel that way about a character. I hope it was intentional. <br><br><br><br><b>Locke:</b><br>I love Locke Lamora. Here we get to see him as a real, multi dimensional person (less perfection does him good). He’s still a scheming genius, but also has fears, hang-ups, and insecurities. We read about a young Locke, the one that didn’t yet quite find himself and an older version that still needs someone (namely Jean) to shake him up from time to time. I’ve always had a thing for intelligent, devious minds, so he’s right up my alley. <br><br><b>Jean:</b><br>Oh my, Jean is one of my favorite characters ever. His loyalty to Locke is staggering. They are a golden combo. He’s not just a sidekick that could disappear without any consequences (like Watson in Sherlock Holmes). Oh no, he is a voice of reason, a steady rock. He is the person that calls Lamora on his bullshit, that doesn’t let Locke wallow in self pity. They need each other. It could even be argued that Locke needs Jean more, than Jean needs Locke. I just love him. (*not enough of Jean in this book. He's just kind of... there)<br><br><b>The humour in those books? </b> One of my favourite things in the whole wide world. Such creative, vulgar insults! I could spend the whole day quoting this book and that still wouldn’t be enough. I love the language. I hate all those Goody Two-Shoes authors that write stories about shining heroes. Stories, in which there is no murder, or theft, or violence, because god forbid our protagonist did something immoral! <b> Here were faced with practicality. People die, people still, some are selfish assholes and there is no noble way of getting around them. That was one of things that impressed me in those books, and it’s still present here. </b> One of the things redeeming that book, I'd say.<br><br>A fair warning – I don’t recommend reading <i> The Republic of Thieves </i> before getting through previous parts. You know that thing most series do? The one where you have all things previous explained? It’s not there. At all. I have no idea how it would read without that prior knowledge, but the way we got it is the way I prefer it. <br><br><br><b>
  <u>What didn't work out in that book?</u>
</b><br><br>- if we were supposed to like Sabetha... She's Locke's obsession, but certainly not love. The word 'love' should never be used around those two. I believe many people would prefer a world in which she dies or doesn't exist at all. <b>She has absolutely no redeeming qualities. </b> Since both storylines were focused on Locke-Sabetha relations, it takes away from what made Gentleman Bastards series awesome. In the end I just really wanted to hit her. It was almost as if she lived to spoil a good thing (disclaimer: I don't need to like characters to enjoy reading about them, so I've survived. Just try looking at her as a curious piece of roadkill.) Self-obsessed queen bitch. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380423583ra/843922.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>- Locke is NOT in love with Sabetha, he's obsessed. I got worried at the very beginning when he had a crush on her as a 5 year old, but I thought "It could work, right?" Well, it didn't (unless that was the point). It's fine for him to be obsessed, but there also comes a time to MOVE ON. She turns Lamora into stumbling, mumbling idiot. Remember kids, repetition without progress is death. He should either get better at handling her over the years or their love should be believable. It's neither. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380423583ra/843923.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>-<b>Main 'plot' (current timeline) gets neglected in favour of 'relationship stuff'. It's barely there and not very much in keeping with genius mastermind we're used to. </b> The plot set in the past is better because there is more scheming (believe it or not) and they're just trying to find themselves. They're learning, and that makes it exciting. There is actually more going on in the recollection of the past than in the present (but I guess anything is better than NOTHING). <br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br><br>-<b> What could be forgiven young Locke is not going to fly for a current version. It'd be much more interesting to see how their relationship changed, rather than how it remained the same. </b><br><br><br><b>The book is redeemed be language, humour, and Gentlemanly Bastardy (whatever little of it we get to see). The pieces of world-building were interesting (as always) but book fell short of what we all came for. </b> I can't rate it lower, because despite all the problems I did enjoy some of it. For the writing alone, for all the jokes and quotes it deserves a biggest of high fives. What I loved was there, just not enough and overshadowed by Sabetha (Habetha - that's what I call her, in Polish it means an old, pitiful sorry excuse of a horse) <br><br><br><b>In the end Scott Lynch remains one of my favourite authors. I’ll await his next books impatiently.</b> I do hope that The Republic of Thieves is just a prep for the next one and all those things mentioned above were intentional. <br><br><br>EDIT: All my criticizing may have made the message a little muddy. <b> I liked the book (a bit). I did enjoy reading it. I did impatiently await every next move of characters. </b> But I'm already emotionally invested into the story and characters. The book had some faults (serious ones). That's all I'm saying. (Three stars means 'liked it' according to goodreads ratings. It's not negative - but if it was the first one of the series for me, the rating would be 1,5 stars. Maybe two if I were in a giving mood.) If this book is good or not we'll know only when the next part comes out. <br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="561770931624784467" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1602542586" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1602542586" />
    <a title="Orient" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43587353-orient"><img alt="Orient" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500791761p2/43587353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1602542586?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Orient" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Orient" href="/user/show/43587353-orient">Orient</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17697801-the-republic-of-thieves">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">action lovers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Orient by: </span>
      Milda Page Runner
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=desperado">desperado</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=recs-by-milda">recs-by-milda</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=killer">killer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=entertaining">entertaining</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=hero">hero</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1602542586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8995427379555076639">Gentleman Bastards books are special and unforgettable to me for a good reason: Mr. Lynch used a strong, fun storyline that kept me hooked. "Republic of Thieves" has two branches in a storyline and it is a fun read too. The two stories blend perfectly with the events helping to reveal one another. I think it's a complicated trick to present a story, but Lynch does it skillfully. The main star of this novel is the political intrigue and the Bastards do it nicely with their sly and shrewd characte</span>
  <span id="freeText8995427379555076639" style="display:none">Gentleman Bastards books are special and unforgettable to me for a good reason: Mr. Lynch used a strong, fun storyline that kept me hooked. "Republic of Thieves" has two branches in a storyline and it is a fun read too. The two stories blend perfectly with the events helping to reveal one another. I think it's a complicated trick to present a story, but Lynch does it skillfully. The main star of this novel is the political intrigue and the Bastards do it nicely with their sly and shrewd characters to run the show.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460644646i/18770133._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I really enjoyed the past and present relationship between Locke and Sabetha (at last!). Oh and I just want to know more and more about her in the series. She is a great match to Locke, so tough, clever and sly. Luv ya gurl &lt;3 There was a darker shade that played in the relationship between Locke and Sabetha, and it was really interesting to see the differences between the past and present, as I could watch the growth of the main characters. But still I had to wonder why their teasing relationship-game went on for so long. Why not remain together at last. As their relationship went back and forth, it left me in a weird mood: I enjoyed the book truly, especially the writing, but at the same time, I found myself stuck to continue forward, because of the teasing in the relationship and a small lack of sparks in the storyline. I expected more unexpected twists and turns from the three Bastards, fighting in politics. I think Gentleman Bastards didn't shine in their full glory. The ending was thrilling and so unexpected, but Locke and Jean didn't play the main parts there. Their ending was a little bit easy and simple. The return of the greatest enemy of the Gentleman Bastards was awesome. It outshined Locke and Jean to me in some way.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460644700i/18770138._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>But still "The Republic of Thieves” is a great book and I am interested in how the story of Locke Lamora, Sabetha and Jean will continue, as I loved the characters. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460644646i/18770134.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="8995427379555076639" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10486192460349541598" style="display:none"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/515752.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="http://gosureviews.blogspot.de/2014/07/republic-of-thiefs-die-republik-der.html" rel="nofollow noopener">German Review on Gosureviews</a><br><br>After 6 years I expected a better story. <br>Sabetha, teased in the previous two books, turns out to be a very weak and shallow character. One of the main plot lines, their "love story" just doesn't work. They don't really have any chemistry together and later in the book I actually got annoyed whenever they had a scene together. <br>It started very strong, but the main story was utterly boring and predictable, so much that I had a hard time finishing the book. The end made up for it a little though. We get some interesting revelations there, but it's rather a setup for Scott Lynchs next book "The Thorn of Emberlain". <br>I guess for a lot of fans who waited so long for this release it will be a big disappointment. <br></span>

<div id="review_1709446141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1709446141" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1709446141?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=bro-mantic">bro-mantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=witches-warlocks-and-magic">witches-warlocks-and-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1709446141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7098978784188139827"><b>We are back on track!!!</b><br/><br/>I don’t have time for a super in depth review but let’s just say that some of the magic that was lost for me in Red Seas over Red Skies is now back again. <br/><br/>Part of the reason is the flashbacks to when Locke and Jean were kids running scams and seeing Sabatha when she was part of their team. The other reason is Sabatha now. SHE IS AMAZING!!! You are either going to love her or hate her but I love her and I love Locke’s reactions to her.<br/><blockquote>
  <i>“I’m, uh, going up to the room … to </i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText7098978784188139827" style="display:none"><b>We are back on track!!!</b><br /><br />I don’t have time for a super in depth review but let’s just say that some of the magic that was lost for me in Red Seas over Red Skies is now back again. <br /><br />Part of the reason is the flashbacks to when Locke and Jean were kids running scams and seeing Sabatha when she was part of their team. The other reason is Sabatha now. SHE IS AMAZING!!! You are either going to love her or hate her but I love her and I love Locke’s reactions to her.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I’m, uh, going up to the room … to get ready.” <br />“You’ve got at least four hours before we have to leave.” <br />“Yeah, but if I don’t start my nervous pacing now, I’ll never have it all done in time.”</i>
</blockquote><br />The other reason was the competition between Sabatha, Locke and Jean. Each has been commissioned by the bonds magi in a political game trying to win an election. I loved the games that they played with each other as Locke and Jean are pitted against Sabetha. It was a funny game and I loved all the one upping they did against each other. It was a great game.<br /><br />Still there are some big revelations about Locke and where he might have come from. Is it true….was it a farce. I still have no idea because it could go either way at this point.<br /><br />Lynch has some great lines and banter throughout this book and I was able to follow along with his story so much better this time around. It seemed like he had a clear idea where his story was going and I loved the journey that he took me on. Plus we are left with a very unexpected ending that made me want to continue on right then….but alas just a little longer until the next book is out.<br /><br />Some of my favorite lines were:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Butterflies instantly came to life in his stomach, and the little bastards were heavily armed.”<br /><br />“My disinterest in your bullshit is so tangible you could make bricks out of it” <br />“Well … damn. You’re obviously in a mood.”<br /> “Am I?” There was danger in her tone. “Am I really? Why should that be exceptional? A boy may be as disagreeable as he pleases, but when a girl refuses to crap sunshine on command the world mutters darkly about her moods.”<br /><br />“You’ve the presence of a mouse fart in a high wind. Stand aside, and try not to catch fire if I shed sparks of genius.”</i>
</blockquote><br />If you were on the fence like I was after Red Seas Under Red Skies I say give this a go as I think that we are back to the brilliance of the original Lies of Locke Lamora.					<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7098978784188139827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1850477212" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1850477212" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1850477212?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1850477212" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8218554347541530623"><blockquote>
  <i>"You're trying to be charming again," she said softly, "but I choose not to be charmed, Locke Lamora."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Long last, after three hefty books, we <b>finally meet Locke's lost love, Sabetha Belacoros.</b><br/><br/>Quick crash course for those with short-term memory loss: Sabetha was a Gentleman Bastard and is hinted to be romantically involved with Locke, and then left for some unknown reason. Locke still loves her, but is slightly bitter about it. <br/><br/>That's from the first two books. In this one, we finally meet the </span>
  <span id="freeText8218554347541530623" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"You're trying to be charming again," she said softly, "but I choose not to be charmed, Locke Lamora."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Long last, after three hefty books, we <b>finally meet Locke's lost love, Sabetha Belacoros.</b><br><br>Quick crash course for those with short-term memory loss: Sabetha was a Gentleman Bastard and is hinted to be romantically involved with Locke, and then left for some unknown reason. Locke still loves her, but is slightly bitter about it. <br><br>That's from the first two books. In this one, we finally meet the elusive woman and get more insight into their past, the rough beginnings of a romance that we know ends in heartbreak. We don't actually get to the heartbreak part, but what's here is plenty telling on its own.<br><br>So, Sabetha herself. I suspect she's going to be one of those characters you <b>either love or hate.</b> The odds are stacked pretty firmly against her. We're used to Locke being the wilest motherfucker around and then she comes along and runs circles around him. She resists Locke's charms and he gets sad and you just want to shake her by the shoulders and go "Fucking kiss already!" because it's obvious she likes him back.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1485663127ra/21837107.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And she's very, <i>very</i> close to being a Pixie Girl. Lynch toed the line extremely fine. She's mysterious and beautiful and intelligent. Her POV appears just once in this sprawling series; most of the time, we see her through Locke's besotted perspective. It's hard to get a grip on her as a living breathing person.<br><br>But once you get past the POV problem, Sabetha is a joy to read. She's resourceful, she demands what's hers, she's insanely, scarily clever. Most misgivings towards her can be resolved if you <b>see things from her perspective,</b> which Sabetha tries to impart on Locke's thick head. Readers want her on a pedestal because that's what Locke wants, or thinks he wants, but Sabetha isn't ever going to be that girl. She <i>will</i> call him out on his bullshit, like his automatic assumption of leadership or his obsession with her red hair. Her refusal to be charmed by Locke can be forgiven, even though it's incredibly frustrating. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Sloppy idiot,” Sabetha muttered at last. “You’re trying to be charming. Well, I do not choose to be charmed by you, Locke Lamora.” </i>
</blockquote><br><br>That line is iconic. If Gentleman Bastards is ever made into a movie or TV series, it will be Sabetha's "You know nothing, Jon Snow."<br><br>I have mixed feelings on the ending. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Locke is the reincarnation of a powerful Bondsmage. He died trying to bring his wife back to life, who had red hair, and basically confirms Sabetha's worst fears, that Locke loves her because she's an object, not a person. <br><br>Part of the reason I love this series is its focus on ordinary people. No queens seeking to reclaim their kingdoms, no kings gathering troops to topple a usurper. Just a gang of orphans, richer and cleverer than anyone else. But if anyone can reconcile two of fantasy's biggest tropes—the Chosen One and Destined Love—it's Lynch. He can have my car, I trust him that much. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I began this series to combat <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23437156.Six_of_Crows__Six_of_Crows___1_" title="Six of Crows (Six of Crows, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Six of Crows</a> withdrawal. To continue comparing it to Bardugo's masterpiece isn't fair to my beloved Bastards, their wisecracks, and crazy schemes. Gentleman Bastards is an amazing series in its own right. I can scarcely wait for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8074907.The_Thorn_of_Emberlain__Gentleman_Bastard___4_" title="The Thorn of Emberlain (Gentleman Bastard, #4) by Scott Lynch" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thorn of Emberlain</a>.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1814327383" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of The Lies of Locke Lamora</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1850477182" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of Red Seas Under Red Skies</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8218554347541530623" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2045817638" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2045817638" />
    <a title="Solseit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57608403-solseit"><img alt="Solseit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501748227p2/57608403.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2045817638?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Solseit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Solseit" href="/user/show/57608403-solseit">Solseit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2045817638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16936401103440994960">Finally I sit down to write a thoughtful (let's say, trying to) review of the book.<br/><br/>This is just the best book yet on Locke and Jean. We are at a point in which we know the two are the closest buddies ever. They are (and continue to be) the priority on everything and everyone for each other. <br/><br/>Their dialogues are pure gold. I was listening to the audiobook while at the gym and I would giggle or laugh every now and again and people would stare at me as if I was crazy. The jury is still out there on </span>
  <span id="freeText16936401103440994960" style="display:none">Finally I sit down to write a thoughtful (let's say, trying to) review of the book.<br /><br />This is just the best book yet on Locke and Jean. We are at a point in which we know the two are the closest buddies ever. They are (and continue to be) the priority on everything and everyone for each other. <br /><br />Their dialogues are pure gold. I was listening to the audiobook while at the gym and I would giggle or laugh every now and again and people would stare at me as if I was crazy. The jury is still out there on my mental sanity but the dialogues are undeniably hilarious. <br />Also, my reading love to Jean is not chipped one bit; I think he is one of the fantasy characters I would always want to have by my side in real life. <br /><br />I love how we get to see a lot more of the Bondismage - the book reveals a lot and infers there is much more to know about the mages and about Locke. But is it all truthful?<br /><br />Also, this is the first time we really experience and get to know Beth. Finally we see Locke and Beth and their magnetic interaction. They are an absolute delight to read and develop (and how they are pretty much living their relationship as an elastic). <br /><br />Another point worth noting is that finally the Sansa brothers are back; I was not expecting to have such an emotional reaction to their appearance but I wish they were still an integral part of the adult story. True, there is so much more to know and discover but I miss them, I miss what they can be and what they could have become. <br /><br />I cannot wait for book 4. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16936401103440994960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229468313?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Artemas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Artemas" href="/user/show/6751111-artemas">Artemas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575084469" href="/book/show/5660854-the-republic-of-thieves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6751111-artemas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6751111-artemas?shelf=600-749-pages">600-749-pages</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229468313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15494477292848821456"><i>Crooked Warden, Nameless Thirteenth, guide Scott Lynch’s pen swiftly through Locke Lamora’s next daring adventure. Grant him new ways of tickling my fancy with poetic swearing, witty scheming, and vicious storytelling.</i><br/><br/>So apparently the Nameless Thirteenth enjoys pissing on mortals and laughing at their prayers. <b>THIS</b> is what I’ve been waiting years for? <b>THIS</b> didn’t even have the same feel as the first two books in the beloved <i>Gentlemen Bastards</i> series. It felt more like a PG-13 version of an R ra</span>
  <span id="freeText15494477292848821456" style="display:none"><i>Crooked Warden, Nameless Thirteenth, guide Scott Lynch’s pen swiftly through Locke Lamora’s next daring adventure. Grant him new ways of tickling my fancy with poetic swearing, witty scheming, and vicious storytelling.</i><br /><br />So apparently the Nameless Thirteenth enjoys pissing on mortals and laughing at their prayers. <b>THIS</b> is what I’ve been waiting years for? <b>THIS</b> didn’t even have the same feel as the first two books in the beloved <i>Gentlemen Bastards</i> series. It felt more like a PG-13 version of an R rated movie … and only because of the swearing … which was great, but not enough to carry the story along.<br /><br /><i>The Republic of Thieves</i> isn’t a trainwreck by any means; more like a lazy hayride when I was expecting a roller coaster. <br /><br />A good 300 pages of this book deals with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Locke/Jean’s political competition with Sabetha, who incidentally is annoying as hell. This was fun at first but quickly became boring and dragged the story along. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Locke just seemed a bit "whipped" by Sabetha, and it got old fast.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://vignette1.wikia.nocookie.net/glee/images/f/f8/Whoopah_whip_whipped_whoosh_friends_burn_chandler.gif/revision/latest?cb=20140325000342">http://vignette1.wikia.nocookie.net/g...</a><br /><br />If <i>The Lies of Locke Lamora</i> had been structured like this book I probably would have passed on the entire series. I'll still read anything Scott Lynch writes, but this was far from his best work.<br /><br />*Kraken unleashed<br /><br />Get your copy here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://amzn.to/2IzcLNf">https://amzn.to/2IzcLNf</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_967744213" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/967744213" />
    <a title="Will M." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20408288-will-m"><img alt="Will M." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452951660p2/20408288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/967744213?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will M." href="/user/show/20408288-will-m">Will M.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473202894" href="/book/show/20955368-the-republic-of-thieves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer967744213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9583645581319332000"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> Blessed is the one who aids a thief, hides a thief, revenges a thief, and remembers a thief, for they shall inherit the night. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I used to think of the Gentleman Bastard series as a mediocre series, but this third instalment finally managed to impress me. Action wise, this had quite a few. Not enough to fully impress me, but quite adequate to keep things interesting. This novel felt more like a character development novel for Locke and the ever mysterious Sabetha.<br/><br/>So we finally get to </span>
  <span id="freeText9583645581319332000" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> Blessed is the one who aids a thief, hides a thief, revenges a thief, and remembers a thief, for they shall inherit the night. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />I used to think of the Gentleman Bastard series as a mediocre series, but this third instalment finally managed to impress me. Action wise, this had quite a few. Not enough to fully impress me, but quite adequate to keep things interesting. This novel felt more like a character development novel for Locke and the ever mysterious Sabetha.<br /><br />So we finally get to know who Sabetha is, and not only that, but we also get to know their past. We finally understand why Locke is so obsessed with her. Just like his first two novels, we have 2 alternating chapters of current events and the interludes. Just like before, I also liked the interludes in this novel. I really liked Father Chains in the fist novel, and it's quite refreshing to read more of him in the third one. As for Sabetha, she's exactly how I envisioned her. Playing hard to get in the beginning, but falls for the guy anyway. I'm not saying it's a bad thing, just that I saw it coming. Jean was quite as interesting as he was in the previous novels. Locke and Jean will always be one of my favorite characters in the fantasy genre.<br /><br />Plot wise, this one kind of lost its track. Lynch tried to incorporate the romance and the plot, but he kind of focused on the romance instead. I would've hated this because of that, but Locke and Sabetha's story was just really interesting to read about. I didn't find it cliche, because of the witty things Father Chains did to them, or made them do. This is a wonderful adventure-fantasy novel with an amazing set of characters. This is way better than the second book, and by a long shot. I'm just really impressed by how Lynch managed to keep my interest for 721 pages. It's not the longest Fantasy novel I've read, but I guess it's one of the best. It didn't make it to my favorites list though, but clearly this one deserves the 5 star rating. <br /><br />While I previously stated that this one focused on the romance, the author still managed to incorporate his natural wit and write with such impeccable technique. The way the romance was written is not the typical cliche romance of two characters you mostly read about. It's filled with adventure, and managed to be a page turner. You would want to know what will happen next. His ever present plot twists were also evident, and that ending was perfect. The latter part was full of plot twists chapter after chapter, and I honestly didn't see them coming. The epilogue was perfect. He couldn't have written a better cliffhanger. I hate and love him for that. The ending of the book itself though, prior to the epilogue, was even better. What is Locke going to do next? Why did the author give him such a terrible fate. I have to know what's going to happen next. An arc copy of the fourth novel would be greatly appreciated.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The novel keeps going back and forth with Locke and Sabetha breaking up and getting back together. The reasons why they did though were really interesting. Like I said, not our cliche type of romance.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />Most of my friends rated this 4 stars, and I understand why. I believe most of them loved the first and second novel, but I didn't. I was even expecting to hate this third one because I got bored with the second. It's all opposite now because they rated the first and second 5, and I rated those two with 4 and 3. Of the three novels currently published, this is the only one that managed to really impress me. I didn't get bored while reading, so that's a good thing. The plot is really good and the characters are amazing. 5/5 stars from me, and I can't wait for the next novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9583645581319332000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer11889530156549313069">Of the three books in the Gentleman Bastard series (Will there ever be any more?) I liked this one least. I really loved meeting Sabetha finally, and seeing Locke and her past. I also loved that we get more information on Locke's mysterious past. I wish this one had kept up the same sense of urgency and suspense that the first two books had though. I wasn't as captivated by the plot because this one focused so much on Locke and Sabetha's perpetually strained relationship. I'm looking forward to </span>
  <span id="freeText11889530156549313069" style="display:none">Of the three books in the Gentleman Bastard series (Will there ever be any more?) I liked this one least. I really loved meeting Sabetha finally, and seeing Locke and her past. I also loved that we get more information on Locke's mysterious past. I wish this one had kept up the same sense of urgency and suspense that the first two books had though. I wasn't as captivated by the plot because this one focused so much on Locke and Sabetha's perpetually strained relationship. I'm looking forward to what will happen in the future of the series if the forth book ever comes out. </span>

<div id="review_1270398409" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1270398409" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1270398409?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17697801-the-republic-of-thieves">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1270398409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17514652076761206759">I really enjoyed reading this series. I love the Locke and Jean bromance. And I'm delighted with the humour, though crude, is strangely eloquent. However, the quality of the books seem to be dropping as the series progressed. <br/><br/>As engaging as the plot was, The Republic of Thieves did suffer from really uneven pacing; some setpieces were dragged out, some rushed through. What I did absolutely love from this book was the backstory Interludes which brought the reader back to Locke's much younger days</span>
  <span id="freeText17514652076761206759" style="display:none">I really enjoyed reading this series. I love the Locke and Jean bromance. And I'm delighted with the humour, though crude, is strangely eloquent. However, the quality of the books seem to be dropping as the series progressed. <br /><br />As engaging as the plot was, The Republic of Thieves did suffer from really uneven pacing; some setpieces were dragged out, some rushed through. What I did absolutely love from this book was the backstory Interludes which brought the reader back to Locke's much younger days in Camorr - hence, the joy of having Chains and the Sanza twins back among the pages again. The main reason for this period of backstory was to introduce Sabetha, the mysterious lady love of Locke Lamora. <br /><br />Try as I may, I can't make myself like Sabetha. Yes, she's brilliant enough to give Locke a run for this money; highly capable and strong as far as being the sole female GB should be. She's also extremely moody, unreasonably so at times, and reduced Locke to a shadow of himself whenever he's around her. The reason why she treated Locke the way she did actually annoyed instead of making me empathize with her. I accept that she's a teenager then, but it did little to endear me to her character. I'm just glad that their interaction in the current-day chapters was much more mature. <br /><br />Jean Tannen, the most loyal friend one can ever have, bar none. His relationship with Locke was the highlight of the series and while he is always protective of his friend, he does not shy away from calling him out on his crap. If I'm asked to describe Jean with one word, it will be - solid!<br /><br />The mystery behind Locke's true identity was also revealed in this book. While quite jawdropping, it was laced with uncertainties given the circumstance of the revelation and even more so because of the personality who delivered the information. I am suspicious.. and hope that Book 4 is indeed going to be published on 22 September 2016. <br /><br /><i>Thieves prosper, <br />The rich remember, <br />We are thieves among thieves.</i> </span>
  <a data-text-id="17514652076761206759" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_656301972" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/656301972" />
    <a title="Nathan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5238423-nathan"><img alt="Nathan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352775557p2/5238423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/656301972?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathan" href="/user/show/5238423-nathan">Nathan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5238423-nathan?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5238423-nathan?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5238423-nathan?shelf=author-male">author-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5238423-nathan?shelf=rated-4-star">rated-4-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer656301972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14832942087180917312"><a href='http://fantasyreviewbarn.com/?p=548' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Review Barn</a><br/><br/>Spoilers from the first two books guaranteed. <br/><br/><b>Prologue</b><br/><br/>The young man has found a rekindled interest in the fantasy genre. Joe Abercrombie pulled him back in with The First Law. George RR Martin tried to break him. Eagerly the man searches forums for something new, something great, a series to follow for years to come. Making his choice he grabs one of the shelf, thinking “damn that is a long, awkward title.”<br/><br/><b>1</b><br/><br/>The man, slightly older, fires up his Kindle. It is finally here! Eage</span>
  <span id="freeText14832942087180917312" style="display:none"><a href="http://fantasyreviewbarn.com/?p=548" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Review Barn</a><br /><br />Spoilers from the first two books guaranteed. <br /><br /><b>Prologue</b><br /><br />The young man has found a rekindled interest in the fantasy genre. Joe Abercrombie pulled him back in with The First Law. George RR Martin tried to break him. Eagerly the man searches forums for something new, something great, a series to follow for years to come. Making his choice he grabs one of the shelf, thinking “damn that is a long, awkward title.”<br /><br /><b>1</b><br /><br />The man, slightly older, fires up his Kindle. It is finally here! Eagerly he starts reading, looking for answers to old questions. Was Locke really poisoned, if so how will he pull through? Is there any possible way Sabetha will live up to the hype? Can Lynch’s unique writing style stay fresh, particularly the flashbacks? Will the man be just as excited for the fourth book of the series as he was for the third?<br /><br />The early going proves promising. Quickly the man is ensnared in a flashback, complete with an early Sabetha sighting. The author still has the touch; the flashbacks are not intrusive despite the impatience to get to the main story. The flashbacks are a bit different this time around, no longer dealing with major time jumps. Instead, after the prologue dealing with early life, they focus on the full complement of the Gentleman Bastards dealing with one assignment (reviving a theatre in some disrepair). Very much focused on the relationship between Locke and Sabetha, there were plenty of shenanigans to keep readers entertained<br /><br />The flashbacks may be a bit dry for some readers, despite plenty of the usually scheming large sections were still spent dealing with the workings of the theatre and the play being performed. No doubt the play, entitled ‘Republic of Thieves,’ will be devoured by some readers looking for clues hidden within for future story lines. Though the man isn’t one of those, he did enjoy the wit and glimpses of larger story that he saw from the imaginary work.<br /><br /><b>Interlude</b><br /><br />Oh my god was that book awesome. Instantly the young man grabs the sequel. Peaking at the cover synopsis he wrinkles his brow. A Pirate story? How the hell is that going to work?<br /><br /><b>2</b><br /><br />The man, finished all too soon, sits back to gather his thoughts. A rare book that he would have been happy to have another hundred pages of. The flashback storyline was wonderful, felt complete, and was a fun addition to the backstory. But what of the “present day” storyline? Was it everything the man was hoping for? In some ways it was, though he can’t help but thinking it needed…something more in order to feel complete.<br /><br />The main storyline was certainly entertaining. Politics as spectator sport! With Gentleman Bastards playing the game there is no way it couldn’t be fun. But the political game perhaps is best not looked at too deeply; it wasn’t the most convincing set up. And while a deeper look at the vote chasing Locke and Jean must go through may have led to a more bloated book, it might have been a good thing. A lot of double crossing and fun shenanigans for sure, but not much showed how votes were turned or lost in this all important election. For those used to getting the full details of the Bastards complicated plans handed down piece by piece it was a tad disappointing, though by no means a complete let down. Perhaps just a case of unusually high expectations.<br /><br />Learning a bit more about the bondmages is welcome as well. Their participation in the game of politics is perhaps not something to look at too closely, but in most other ways they were fleshed out strong. Why they serve for money, why they don’t run everything with their magics; perhaps not all is explained but details are becoming clearer. It all makes the land Locke lives in a bit more alive; not a place one would want to live in but enthralling to read about.<br /><br /><b>Interlude</b><br /><br />The dinner was good and the evening enjoyable. The man’s little boy is tired, thus the bedtime rituals begin. Teeth are brushed, jammies put on, and hugs are given. One for Mom, one for Dad, and one for the visiting Aunt; the man’s younger sister. Little boy in bed the Aunt realizes she has a long drive ahead and starts to say goodnight. Can she look through the man’s library and borrow a few? What would he recommend? Sounds interesting, I’ll try it. Damn is that a long, awkward title.<br /><br /><b>3</b><br /><br />The man’s thoughts turn to Sabetha. Rarely is there such build up for the unknown, such an important character in the protagonists life yet not seen for two full books. It was asking for a letdown, there was no way she could live up to the hype and expectations readers were building.<br /><br />But she did.<br /><br />She matched Locke hit for hit, mental blow by mental blow, scheme for scheme. She knew when he was going left, knew that he knew that she knew, and caught him the act of faking right and going left anyway. It is perfectly clear why Locke has pined for this woman for five years, their battles of schemes and wits rarely tip to far in one or the others favor, and Sabetha seems to be the only one who gets the better of Locke time and again.<br /><br />As a competitor Sabetha was everything hoped for. As the love of Locke’s life, maybe a little less. She is hard to pin down. One true love, foretold by destiny? Lynch plays with the trope a bit, specifically showing Sabetha’s reluctance to let it decide for her. Almost opposite of a pixie dream girl, she isn’t there to give Locke everything he wants, but often will give him just what he needs. It is easy to foresee a portion of the fandom turning on her; calls of whiney and bitch will be common for her sometimes treatment of Locke. Admittedly at times her extreme mood changes into anger seemed directed at the wrong source. But be clear, it is just one more way she is the perfect counterpart to Locke, no stranger to sudden mood shifts, brooding, and anger himself.<br /><br />Yes, Sabetha will be a nice addition to future books, as long as the formulaic nature of their interactions is changed up a bit next time around. Locke already had a perfect friend in Jean, now he has a perfect foil in Sabetha. She was fun, witty, and razor sharp.<br /><br /><b>4</b><br /><br />Fans of Lynch shouldn’t be disappointed. Closer in style to Lies of Locke Lamora than its sequel, the book moved at the same brisk speed, wove the story between two timelines beautifully, and provided plenty of excitement. Ending on less of a cliff hanger was a plus, though of course there are plenty of open questions to provide fodder for the rest of the series. The flashbacks are interesting, and provide a chance to bring back old friends to the story. The main storyline was fun and exciting, though a bit shallower. Sabetha was worth the wait and Locke and Jean are still an awesome pair. <br /><br />4 stars. Some areas may not pass the logic test, but it is too entertaining to rate lower and was well worth the wait.<br /><br /><b>Epilog</b><br /><br />“Ya, hello.”<br /><br />“Hey Sis, what you doing? Nothing, just driving home”<br /><br />“Oh, you finished it? What did you think?”<br /><br />“What the hell do you mean you didn’t like it? It's one of my favorites!”<br /><br />Review copy acquired from NetGalley.<br /><br />edit: Three months later and I am still finding typos.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14832942087180917312" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5361095427301079293">Seeing as this is the 3rd book in a series, I don't want to say too much about the plot. I will say that I enjoyed this one much more than <i>Red Seas Under Red Skies</i> but still not quite as much as the first book <i>The Lies of Locke Lamora.</i> <br/><br/>I appreciate that we *finally* got to learn more about Sabetha, and the flashbacks in this book, YOU GUYS, the flashbacks were SO good.   <span id="freeText5361095427301079293" style="display:none">Seeing as this is the 3rd book in a series, I don't want to say too much about the plot. I will say that I enjoyed this one much more than <i>Red Seas Under Red Skies</i> but still not quite as much as the first book <i>The Lies of Locke Lamora.</i> <br /><br />I appreciate that we *finally* got to learn more about Sabetha, and the flashbacks in this book, YOU GUYS, the flashbacks were SO good. I loved the theatrical and political aspects of this one a lot. And as always, Locke &amp; Jean are the ultimate BroTP (pretty sure I used that in my review of book 2, but it's true! They're the absolute best). It was hilarious, as all the books in this series are. And overall, a really great time. THAT EPILOGUE THOUGH. So glad I waited to read this one a while after book 2 because it was fun to return to these characters.<br /><br />And now we wait for <i>The Thorn of Emberlain</i>.</span>

<div id="review_1967122382" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1967122382" />
    <a title="ChopinFC" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51633786-chopinfc"><img alt="ChopinFC" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545283749p2/51633786.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1967122382?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ChopinFC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ChopinFC" href="/user/show/51633786-chopinfc">ChopinFC</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1967122382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8810283249715558471"><b>full review...<br/><br/>The Republic of Thieves is yet another outstanding and highly entertaining continuation of the witty, highly sarcastic and definitely R17-rated series Gentleman Bastards!<br/><br/>4 ½ Stars</b><br/><br/>Again, Scott Lynch had me on the floor belly up laughing for most of the series, and trust me ‘The Republic of Thieves’ was just as fun as the previous 2 entries in the series! I’m a big believer of Goodreads, and all the wonderful (and some not so wonderful) reviews in here. Nothing is worse than reading </span>
  <span id="freeText8810283249715558471" style="display:none"><b>full review...<br><br>The Republic of Thieves is yet another outstanding and highly entertaining continuation of the witty, highly sarcastic and definitely R17-rated series Gentleman Bastards!<br><br>4 ½ Stars</b><br><br>Again, Scott Lynch had me on the floor belly up laughing for most of the series, and trust me ‘The Republic of Thieves’ was just as fun as the previous 2 entries in the series! I’m a big believer of Goodreads, and all the wonderful (and some not so wonderful) reviews in here. Nothing is worse than reading a review that will give away spoilers (lamo) . So I am pretty darn careful about skimming through some reviews of books that I am about to read so as not to run that risk. One overall perspective from most reviews about GB 3, is that it had lost it’s ‘ wittiness’ and ‘ kick-assery’ from the first previous books. <br><br><b>Nothing could be further from the truth! Lynch has a delightful warped imagination, and he creates a world of thievery, magic, romance and betrayal in ‘Republic of Thieves’ </b><br><br>The story picks up right where we left off from the 2nd book. We’re back again with Locke and Jean, best of ‘compadres’ and lifelong accomplices, in a completely different type of adventure. This time around, the gang ends up in the dreaded city of <i>Karthain</i>, known for being the home of the <i>‘Bondsmagi’</i>. As some of you may recall, the magi are an incredibly powerful cast of magicians that are able to control minds, teleport into animals and have omnipotent sorcery. Locke and Jean somehow get finagled into meddling with the local politics of Karthain. They are contracted by the magi to scheme and interfere with a local ‘political election’ . <br><br>As most of you may recall, we are left with a big cliffhanger in the end of the second book. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Locke and Jean both are poisoned, and in the end Locke is able to give the only remnant of the antidote to Jean, thus sacrificing his own life to save his friend and brother Jean.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The way Lynch unwraps this problem is quite spectacular! He is able to use sarcasm, very R-17 rated fun, magic and deep rooted emotions all to break away the tension of previous book. The results are astounding! Much like music, where the tension of a minor key or a dissonant sound can be completely resolved by coming back to major key! Lynch’s prose is fun, fast-paced and he creates tension but resolves it brilliantly with humor and deep rooted human emotions .<br><br><b>
  <i> “ Three things must you kiss before I let you spooke me for good. My boots, my balls and my ass” </i>
</b>(spoken eloquently by Locke) <br><br>Lynch takes us back in time with multiple alternating ‘Interlude’ chapters retelling the story of Locke and his apprenticeship in the Gentleman Bastard’s crew. It was very cool to have more exposition on characters such as the ‘Sanza brothers’ as well as Locke and Jean when they were mere teenagers yet to fully blossom. We also revisit ‘Father Chains’, the famous ‘eyeless Priest’ who is the leader of GB, and adopts all of the boys and girl and teaches them the way of priesthood ( more like thievery, connivery and deceit). <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500223525i/23311553._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>*DRUMROLL PLEASE….* We finally get to meet the most talked about, revered, loved and idolized Sabetha!! </b> <br><br>It only took 2 full books and a shitload of pages (1150 pages to be exact) for Lynch to finally introduce us to Sabetha! Unfortunately, the expectation ‘bar’ was set way too high and by the time Sabetha is finally introduced, I could not stop from feeling a sense of disappointment. Don’t mistake me, Sabetha is fire-red haired, passionate and cunning. Yet, it is the way she mistreats Locke Lamora that put me off about her character. After 2 books, I am so damn invested in Locke Lamora and feel like I am his biggest fan ( through all of his misadventures). So here comes Sabetha, beautiful, dangerous yet with Locke she is petulant, arrogant and downright mean. Locke’s fascination for Sabetha leaves me dumfounded. <br><br>	<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500223748i/23311592._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Some things I disliked about the book, was the ‘political’ aspect of their new adventure in the city of Karthain. Compared to the adventures of the ‘Red Seas Under Red Skies’ (GB 2) where the boys are full thick into the world of pirates with all of its fuckery and madness, this one falls flat. Some of the actions Jean and Locke partake to throw off the political ‘election’ are kitty cat in comparison to fighting mid-sea battles inside a pirate’s warship! <br><br>I also did not care much about the some of the retrospective adventures of the GB as they infiltrate a theatrical production and have to participate in a ‘play’. I didn’t think the ‘play’ added much to character development, and it was actually kind of boring. I much rather see the Gentleman Bastard stealing shit, or conniving to heist a big score against a noble family!<br><br>Finally, I listened to the Audiobooks version, narrated by the talented ‘Michael Page’. Again, the <b>Audiobook version of GB 3 is downright FANTASTIC!! </b> I highly recommend for either first time readers of the novel or if you’re in mood for a re-read.<br><br><b>Lynch does the rare feat of continuing a masterful follow up in the story of Locke and the GB’s adventures! Some details in the story fall flat. However, the series continues to highly entertain; has hilarious near R-17 dialogue, magic, thievery and unforgettable characters which will leave you peeing in your pants! :)<br><br>4 1/2 Stars </b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8810283249715558471" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_459035812" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/459035812" />
    <a title="Jennifer Lim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7829865-jennifer-lim"><img alt="Jennifer Lim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469438055p2/7829865.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/459035812?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Lim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Lim" href="/user/show/7829865-jennifer-lim">Jennifer Lim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780575077010" href="/book/show/5660852-the-republic-of-thieves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7829865-jennifer-lim?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7829865-jennifer-lim?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7829865-jennifer-lim?shelf=grimdark">grimdark</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer459035812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1456915110915036802"> <blockquote>
  <i>Quit being so hard on yourself. We are what we are; we love what we love. We don't need to justify it to anyone... not even to ourselves. </i>
</blockquote><br/>Yes. You are absolutely correct, Locke. So no matter how unhappy I am with this installment, no matter how lovesick you were with Sabetha, no matter how thinner this book's plot is compared with the first two, no matter how bored I felt when Patience is talking, I am still giving this four stars, because gods damn it, I am so biased when it comes to Lynch</span>
  <span id="freeText1456915110915036802" style="display:none"> <blockquote>
  <i>Quit being so hard on yourself. We are what we are; we love what we love. We don't need to justify it to anyone... not even to ourselves. </i>
</blockquote><br>Yes. You are absolutely correct, Locke. So no matter how unhappy I am with this installment, no matter how lovesick you were with Sabetha, no matter how thinner this book's plot is compared with the first two, no matter how bored I felt when Patience is talking, I am still giving this four stars, because gods damn it, I am so biased when it comes to Lynch's witty writing and I don't think I can possibly not like anything with his name on it.<br><br>It's still entertaining, still witty and funny, and it will make you swoon. This is all about Locke and Sabetha's courtship, both in the past and the present. If you wanted to meet this red headed girl and know why Locke is so fixated on her, you will not be disappointed. If you wanted the scheming Locke fixated on a good haul, well then, better re-read the first two books. <br><br>The Republic of Thieves sets the stage for the future books' plotlines. Expect twists regarding Locke's real identity, the return of a foe, and well, Sabetha. All in all, it's not that bad, but even the enlightenment of Sabetha's character is not enough for Republic of Thieves to be out of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/127455.The_Lies_of_Locke_Lamora__Gentleman_Bastard___1_" title="The Lies of Locke Lamora (Gentleman Bastard, #1) by Scott Lynch" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lies of Locke Lamora</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/887877.Red_Seas_Under_Red_Skies__Gentleman_Bastard___2_" title="Red Seas Under Red Skies (Gentleman Bastard, #2) by Scott Lynch" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Seas Under Red Skies</a>' shadow.<br><br><b>***July 17, 2013 Edit***</b><br><br><b>WHAT?!</b><br><br>Some goodreaders have ARCs already!!!! Dying of envy here, people.<br><br>It's time for a re-read, gentlemen.<br><br><b>***End of edit***<b><br><br><b><i>Crooked Warden, it's Sabetha.</i></b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380398113ra/769016.gif" width="320" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></b></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1456915110915036802" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
