    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2027398022" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2027398022" />
    <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries"><img alt="Mayim de Vries" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560508357p2/50424456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2027398022?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mayim de Vries" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries">Mayim de Vries</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2027398022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13336043799071926693">Without any doubts <b>Gentleman Bastards is one of my favourite series to date even though from instalment to instalment it steadily goes down the slope</b> with the full quintuple fuckdamn of stars for <a>The Lies of Locke Lamora</a> , three and a half star aboard for the <a>Red Seas Under Red Skies</a> and <b>three very conflicted stars here.</b> <br/><br/>If you remember, I had a feeling that the previous instalment of Gentleman Bastards was the book proper an accompanying pirate novella. Now, the <i>Republic of Thieves</i> is also a co</span>
  <span id="freeText13336043799071926693" style="display:none">Without any doubts <b>Gentleman Bastards is one of my favourite series to date even though from instalment to instalment it steadily goes down the slope</b> with the full quintuple fuckdamn of stars for <a>The Lies of Locke Lamora</a> , three and a half star aboard for the <a>Red Seas Under Red Skies</a> and <b>three very conflicted stars here.</b> <br /><br />If you remember, I had a feeling that the previous instalment of Gentleman Bastards was the book proper an accompanying pirate novella. Now, the <i>Republic of Thieves</i> is also a combo novel; it contains two books mashed together intermittently. The first one, the present, picks up promptly where we finished the pirate adventures of Tal Verrar. The second, the past, sheds light onto those golden years in Camorr when all the Gentleman Bastards were in their prime. <br /><br /><b>In the Republic of Thieves Past, present and future walk into a bar and it IS tense.</b> Both have things I loved and things I found wanting. <br /><br />In the present, Locke is dying, his humours terminally imbalanced due to the poisoning and no force on earth able to cure him save the Bondsmagi and those are not sweetly predisposed towards Locke since the unfortunate affair with the Falconer. Do you remember Falconer? Brush up your memory, issues around him are becoming central to the story again. It turns out that Karthain is not as monolithic as we were led to believe in the previous instalments and one of the warring factions offers to <b>save Locke in exchange for a job neatly done: winning the elections. Rigged from top to bottom</b>. <br /><br /><i>“Government affairs are a bit beyond our experience,” said Jean.<br />“Nonsense. You’ll feel right at home. What is government but theft by consent? You’ll be moving in a society of kindred spirits.”</i><br /><br />Oh, and have I mentioned that Sabetha their chief opponent in this game?<b>Book one was the tale of revenge, book two gave us a story of friendship, this time we are given a romance.</b><br /><br />The romance rules both the past and the present. In the former, Locke and Sabetha come together, in the latter, they come to terms. Or try to, at least. I am not happy at all with the way this was played. <br /><br /><b>The past has no conclusion to the story, there is no point, no morale, no ending. Even the buildup in terms of explaining the background of the romance was lacking</b> (we still don’t know the details of the initial breakup). The main strength of the interludes was that it is marvellous to read about the whole gang alive and kicking. In terms of the Sabetha-Locke affair, the interludes were clumsily done with loads of unnecessary details and as such they read more like a prequel than the genius intervals of the first instalment. <br /><br />The present is better in terms of pacing and emotional whirlwind but the way it ends is perplexing. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Why does she run away? Because she believes that Locke’s inclination towards redheads is just a reincarnated habit not a real love for her? It’s kind of ridiculous. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I was waiting for Sabetha so long and with such apprehension, that I don’t blame Mr Lynch for not being able to meet my expectations. He scattered the innuendos with the precision of a master fencer. He led us to believe that the cosmic love between them is less a case of happy coincidence, more of a tragic destiny. Unfortunately for me, <b>when Sabetha is deprived of her mystery shroud, she turns out to be an utter disappointment</b>. For me, Mr Lynch has failed to convey the image of wonder, I cannot look at Sabetha through Locke’s eyes. I don’t see in her the miracle she purportedly is. She does not convince me. What I see is an arrogant girl, a cruel perfectionist with her conscience sensibly trimmed and a functionalist approach to life whereby everything and everyone else is just a tool to advance her own agenda. She has her moments, true, but overall, she is just an annoyance. <br /><br /><i>“A boy may be as disagreeable as he pleases, but when a girl refuses to crap sunshine on command the world mutters darkly about her moods.”</i><br /><br /><b>What I liked about the <i>Republic of Thieves</i> is that it gives the reader another layer of the story and the worldbuilding. We are invited to reconsider the things we think we know about the world and the things we take for granted</b> - like the Elders and their sudden disappearance. This becomes a very important motif and a new element to the puzzle. I like the way Mr Lynch shows different facets of the same story in each book adding a new hue here and a new perspective there. It gives us a complex world, a world that is not black and white. <br /><br />The electoral shenanigans in Karthain are fun to read, even if we read them with the feeling that none of this matters truly. The whole geopolitical conundrum of the Iron Sea is just a background to the character-driven story. It is all about Locke, nothing more and nothing less. But the turn Locke’s life takes is questionable, though I am willing to give Mr Lynch benefit of the doubt and assume he can pull this through. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[in my mind I have already appropriated Locke as the lost Vardan heir, not as a creepy emanation of a power-hungry mage! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Future looks dark and there are things moving and dreaming in the darkness. Let’s hope the Thorn of Emberlain will give us answers. <br /><br />—<br />My review of <a>The Lies of Locke Lamora</a>.<br />My review of <a>Red Seas Under Red Skies</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13336043799071926693" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1791449569" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1791449569" />
    <a title="Teal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60821533-teal"><img alt="Teal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581808227p2/60821533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1791449569?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Teal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Teal" href="/user/show/60821533-teal">Teal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17697801-the-republic-of-thieves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60821533-teal?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60821533-teal?shelf=sff">sff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60821533-teal?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60821533-teal?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60821533-teal?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60821533-teal?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60821533-teal?shelf=hated-it">hated-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60821533-teal?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60821533-teal?shelf=mc-on-ace-spectrum">mc-on-ace-spectrum</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60821533-teal?shelf=this-never-happened">this-never-happened</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1791449569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4305981535816140819">To the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29588376-the-lies-of-locke-lamora' rel='nofollow noopener'> 1st book in the series</a>: 5 stars, and a spot on my All-Time Favorite Fantasy Novels list.<br/><br/>To the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40604556-red-seas-under-red-skies' rel='nofollow noopener'>2nd in the series</a>: 4 stars, and a hearty recommendation.<br/><br/>To this, the 3rd in the series: 1 star, and an earnest plea to the author to <i>never</i> try to make a career at writing romance.<br/><br/>I waited for this book for years -- and once I had it in my hands (pretty much the first moment it became available), it took me years to finish it. How many years? I'm not sure, exactly -- I know it was more than two,</span>
  <span id="freeText4305981535816140819" style="display:none">To the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29588376-the-lies-of-locke-lamora" rel="nofollow noopener"> 1st book in the series</a>: 5 stars, and a spot on my All-Time Favorite Fantasy Novels list.<br /><br />To the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40604556-red-seas-under-red-skies" rel="nofollow noopener">2nd in the series</a>: 4 stars, and a hearty recommendation.<br /><br />To this, the 3rd in the series: 1 star, and an earnest plea to the author to <i>never</i> try to make a career at writing romance.<br /><br />I waited for this book for years -- and once I had it in my hands (pretty much the first moment it became available), it took me years to finish it. How many years? I'm not sure, exactly -- I know it was more than two, and less than five. So let's say 3. Three years to read this -- this -- this <i>thing</i> I'd been so eagerly anticipating. And I only managed to reach The End because I finally gave myself permission to skim/skip the boring parts. Turns out it was <i>all</i> boring parts. Neither of the two storylines, past nor present, captured my interest. And keep in mind that I went into this with the highest possible level of enthusiasm, eager and ready to be pleased. <br /><br />That the story is profoundly boring is far from the worst thing about it. No, that distinction belongs to the absolutely excruciating, cringe-inducing attempt to portray the mysterious Grand Romance between Locke and his One True Love. OMG, has there ever been such a pair of juvenile ninnies pretending to have a Grand Passion? My vocabulary fails me; there's no way I can convey the trite and puerile nature of their interactions. Ugh, when I say it was cringe-inducing I mean that literally -- I physically cringed and grimaced and shrank into myself as I read their scenes together. <br /><br />So bad. It was all so, so bad. There were no redeeming features to this book whatsoever. I'm not sure I've ever experienced a series that tanked so hard, so fast. If the 4th book is ever written, I don't think my joy in books 1 and 2 will be sufficient to make me willing to pick it up and revisit these characters. Sorry, Jean -- I'll miss you, but everyone else in this world has worn out their welcome. And then some.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4305981535816140819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ahn4bUZf8uV9Jt/Ow2jw4RU6MrhQcNT1kY4ULlgG7p4QwEWfPCYygAyjcGgup0Drbh7vLex3IiEj/MgzW8QoFw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5oI6N51LjF19oDi8PT9/4CJZY44WNCVcDUanrGuRZvH0W4fF5zJMOAwllxrQ8M/qWX2+G6oz04i/NHuxaFOgeA==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer418549034438228246">I was born in St. Paul, Minnesota on April 2, 1978, the first of three brothers. I've lived in the Minneapolis/St. Paul area my entire life; currently, just across the border in Wisconsin, about half an hour east of the Twin Cities.<br/><br/><i>The Lies of Locke Lamora,</i> my first novel, was bought by Simon Spanton at Orion Books in August, 2004. Prior to that I had just about every job you usually see in this s</span>
  <span id="freeText418549034438228246" style="display:none">I was born in St. Paul, Minnesota on April 2, 1978, the first of three brothers. I've lived in the Minneapolis/St. Paul area my entire life; currently, just across the border in Wisconsin, about half an hour east of the Twin Cities.<br /><br /><i>The Lies of Locke Lamora,</i> my first novel, was bought by Simon Spanton at Orion Books in August, 2004. Prior to that I had just about every job you usually see in this sort of author bio-- dishwasher, busboy, waiter, web designer, office manager, prep cook, and freelance writer. I trained in basic firefighting at Anoka Technical College in 2005, and became a volunteer firefighter in June of that year.<br /><br />In 2007 <i>The Lies of Locke Lamora</i> was a World Fantasy Award finalist. <br /><br />In 2008 I received the Sydney J. Bounds Best Newcomer Award from the British Fantasy Society.<br /><br />In 2010, I lost a marriage but gained a cat, a charming ball of ego and fuzz known as Muse (Musicus Maximus Butthead Rex I). <br /><br />My partner, the lovely and critically acclaimed SF/F writer Elizabeth Bear, lives in Massachusetts. </span>
